Record #14
  cipher_text: Encode the following text to a Caesar cipher. The shift is 6.
plain text: καλλιεργήστε τις σχέσεις σας
Shift: 6
Encrypted text: ονδξίωξηστε τς ρχέσεις σας
Decrypted text: καλλιεργήστε τις σχέσεις σας
Note: The Greek alphabet is used in this example.
Caesar Cipher is a type of substitution cipher where each letter in the plaintext is'shifted' a certain number of places down the alphabet. For example, a shift of  a letter 'a' with a shift of 1 would result in 'b'. The method is named after Julius Caesar, who reportedly used it to communicate with his officials.
To encode the text, the following steps are taken:
1. Convert each letter of the plaintext to its corresponding numerical value using the standard ordering of the Greek alphabet (α=1,, β=2, γ=3, …,, ω=24).
2. Add the shift value to each numerical value.
3. Convert the resulting numerical values back to their corresponding letters.
To decode the text, the following steps are taken:
1. Convert each letter of the ciphertext to its corresponding numerical value using the standard ordering of the Greek alphabet (α=1, β=2, γ=3, …, ω=24).
2. Subtract the shift value from each numerical value.
3. Convert the resulting numerical values back to their corresponding letters.
In this example, the shift value is 6. Therefore, the encoding and decoding process is as follows:
Encoding:
κα (20) -> κα+6 = υ (26)
λλ (30) -> λλ+6 = ο (36)
ι (10) -> ι+6 = μ (16)
ε (5) -> ε+6 = ζ (11)
ρ (18) -> ρ+6 = χ (24)
γή (7) -> γ+6 = ι (13)
σ (19) -> σ+6 = ω (25)
τ (20) -> τ+6 = υ (26)
ε (5) -> ε+6 = ζ (11)
σ (19) -> σ+6 = ω (25)
χ (22) -> χ+6 = ψ (28)
έ (8) -> έ+6 = θ (14)
σ (19) -> σ+6 = ω (25)
σ (19) -> σ+6 = ω (25)
α (1) -> α+6 = ζ (7)
σ (19) -> σ+6 = ω (25)
Decoding:

  cipher_text: Encode the following text to a Caesar cipher. The shift is 6.
plain text: η καλοσύνη δεν κοστίζει τίποτα
plain text in ascii: \u03b7 \u03ba\u03bb\u03bf\u03b9\u03b7\u03b5 \u03b4\u03b5\u03bb\u03bd\u03b9\u03b1\u03b9\u03b1 \u03b4\u03b5\u03b3\u03b9\u03b1\u03b9\u03b4\u03b5\u03b1
I tried to do it like this:

plainText = "\u03b7 \u03ba\u03bb\u03bf\u03b9\u03b7\u03b5 \u03b4\u03b5\u03bb\u03bd\u03b9\u03b1\u03b9\u03b1 \u03b4\u03b5\u03b3\u03b9\u03b1\u03b9\u03b4\u03b5\u03b1"
def caesar_cipher(plainText, shift):
    cipherText = ""
    for char in plainText:
        if char.isalpha():
            ascii_offset = ord('a') if char.islower() else ord('A')
            encrypted_char = chr((ord(char) - ascii_offset + shift) % 26 + ascii_offset)
            cipherText += encrypted_char
        else:
            cipherText += char
    return cipherText
print(caesar_cipher(plainText, 6))

But I get the following error:

UnicodeEncodeError: 'charmap' codec can't encode character '\u03b7' in position 0: character maps to <undefined>

How can I solve this?
